Perhaps instead of using int type to identify the different sub tasks, could have Task as a parent class and the other subtasks as a children class

i.e.:
public class Task ``{``
``}``
public class ToDo extends Task ``{``
``}``

Using super classes' toString() in the child's classes' toString is an idea to automate the printing of each task
Task's toString: "[ ] Task A"
Child's toString: "[T]" + super.toString()
Of course this is a very simplified example, it is up to you on how you implement it

`String[] lineWords = userInput.trim().split("\\s+");` Might be better here, as using `line.split(" ")` can cause it to interperet a space as a word, for example if I typed "unmark foobar" with 3 spaces inbetween, it will interperet the middle space as a word, or if I typed "unmark foobar " it will interperet the trailing space as another split and have a third, empty word ""

    ``}``

    for (int i = 0; i < taskCount; i++) ``{``

Issue: String concatenation (+) in toString() creates multiple String objects, which is less efficient.
Suggestion: Use String.format() for better readability and efficiency:
    return String.format("%s (by: %s)", super.toString(), dueDate);

</panel>

<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/42#discussion_r1942311622" expanded>

</div>

Issue: The super(name,"[D]") call lacks spaces after the comma, which is against the coding standard (Section: [Spacing](https://se-education.org/guides/conventions/java/basic.html#layout)).
Suggestion: super(name, "[D]");

</panel>

### 86. HENG..G YI `@HTY2003` (11 comments)
</div>


<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/90#discussion_r1945997687" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**1 :fas-comment:**
</div>

To avoid arrowhead style code, you can consider handling unusual input cases by putting the input handling code for a given command into its own function. After this, you can catch unusual cases and return/end the function early.

E.g. brief pseudocode for function contents

if (unusualCase)
    return;

if (unusualCase2)
    return;

continueHandlingInput();

This will make the code less confusing (although this is a great attempt)
</panel>

`switch (action) ``{```
`case "bye":`

`switch (action) ``{```
`    case "bye" -&gt; exit();`

### 176. T HA..ARAN `@vegetablestabber` (5 comments)
</div>


<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/107#discussion_r1942253586" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**1 :fas-comment:**
</div>

`tasks[i].toString()` can just be `tasks[i]` when concatenating it to a String. It is, of course, more explicit to the reader but the reader can also figure out that the String representation is derived implicity from a `Task` instead.
</panel>

<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/107#discussion_r1942258597" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**2 :fas-comment:**
</div>

I like how you have multiple methods to handle different types of invalid input, but maybe you could also consider throwing an `Exception` and handling it in the function where it is called?

This would allow you to disconnect printing from the error message and delegates the responsibility of handling the error to the method (e.g. `handleDeadlineCommand`) where the method that is throwing the `Exception` (e.g. `printInvalidDeadline`).

I noticed that you only handle errors by printing so shifting the responsibility to the parent method is something else you might find helpful as you can avoid confusion between using `print` or `println` for every error printing method, but I also understand the straightforwardness of your solution.
</panel>

<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/107#discussion_r1942260717" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**3 :fas-comment:**
</div>

Maybe you could consider creating a new function for obtaining parameters from a given input? This might be useful for any future commands which require parameters and could also be used to handle missing parameters, thus reducing the size of methods like `handleDeadlineCommand` and delegating these responsibilities away into other modular methods.
</panel>

<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/107#discussion_r1942262035" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**1 :fas-comment:**
</div>

Instead of using index to keep track of characters in a string, try to use .split to separate content of a string as it avoids creating magic numbers like 5 and 7.
</panel>

<panel  popup-url="https://github.com/nus-cs2113-AY2425S2/ip/pull/148#discussion_r1945950886" expanded>
<div slot="header">

**2 :fas-comment:**
</div>

Instead of having an add... method for each sub-class of a task, you may consider creating an addTask(Task task) method where you instantiate the tasks as the input parameters of the method. This way you can avoid creating a add... method every time you create another sub-class of a task, and therefore improve readability and make your code easier to maintain.
</panel>
